To see max brightness without going outside, shine the flashlight of another phone into the front camera (Dynamic Island area). Also, the white point of the OLED display on the iPhone 14 Pro Max is slightly warm (yes, with Night Shift off). Photographers and artists might notice this when compared to an LCD screen. To fix this, open Settings, go to Accessibility then Display & Text Size and then Color Filters. Turn Filters On and select Color Tint. Set intensity to the far left, and Hue (scroll down to find it) 3/4 of the way to the right. You can shift it a bit left and right to make whites cooler or warmer.

As neat as it is, the dynamic island idea is literally, entirely just a software gimmick integrated into the phone/ other apps. There is no additional hardware required to accommodate its general functionality, which is essentially an integrated, dynamic widget. They could literally do that on the regular 14's, the 13's etc. but just have the widget animations extend from the bottom/ sides of the notch. The only issue would be seamlessly integrating it with multiple applications, but like I said Apple could *absolutely* make that software available to previous iPhones in a software update if they so choose. But we all know they won't, because then the dynamic island concept would become less "exclusive" and lose the illusion that it is only possible on the newest, latest tech.    Also the Non Pro 14 sounds better because Apple had to shove/ squish the speaker module into less space on the Pros in order to fit the scanners/ camera module into the dynamic island space. In the regular 14 and earlier models the bigger notch gave more room for the speaker embedded in the top bezel to dig out a little more space into the overlapping notch. But they couldn't do that with the 14 Pro so they had to compromise the speaker quality in order to lower the notch/ island and its sensor array.

I've always been a believer in never buy the next major changes iPhone, but to always buy the next one after that. Eg: don't buy the 14 but definitely buy the 15, skip the 16 but definitely buy the 17. Never buy the standard but alway buy the pro, pro max and plus versions, always buy the 256gb and higher. The major changes versions always have issues and are tester versions, whereas the one after that is the version that has had those problems solved, upgraded and improved. Eg: don't buy the 12 but definitely get the 13, the 12 was a major change from the 11. The 13 was more a stable version. So in saying all that the 15 will be the more stable version of the 14.

I want no reply on my comment.
The brightness was the same/identical for the two phones indoors because the level you are testing is the real scene 100% window brightness. Essentially this is the max brightness that the entire screen can go up to at once. Since you were on the white screen in the notes app, the screen recognizes the color is covering most of the display and is using 100% of the panel. The 2000 nits apple was referring to is actually the peak brightness which is different. Peak brightness refers to a usually 10% or 5% window of the display which can reach up to 2000 nits on its own. For example, if the sun in a video you're watching is in the top corner of the display, it will reach 2000 nits for the sun alone as it takes up less than a 10% window.
